  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f3070fc5-f0f8-4ca9-ae7f-ae7aebb71a9e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17051228920492621539">The 39 Clues is Scholastic's groundbreaking new series, spanning 10 adrenaline-charged books, 355 trading cards, and an online game where readers play a part in the story. <br/><br/>The 39 Clues books set the story, and the cards, website and game allow kids to participate in it. Kids visit the website - <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.the39clues.com'>www.the39clues.com</a> - and discover they are lost members of the Cahill family. T</span>
  <span id="freeText17051228920492621539" style="display:none">The 39 Clues is Scholastic's groundbreaking new series, spanning 10 adrenaline-charged books, 355 trading cards, and an online game where readers play a part in the story. <br /><br />The 39 Clues books set the story, and the cards, website and game allow kids to participate in it. Kids visit the website - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.the39clues.com">www.the39clues.com</a> - and discover they are lost members of the Cahill family. They set up online accounts where they can compete against other kids and against Cahill characters to find all 39 clues. Through the website, kids can track their points and clues, manage their card collections, dig through the Cahill archives for secrets, and "travel" the world to collect Cahill artifacts, interview characters, and hunt down clues. Collecting cards helps: Each card is a piece of evidence containing information on a Cahill, a clue, or a family secret.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8168505694540898401">My review is really 4.5 stars for a couple reasons. First, it has a good setup, a bunch of different authors create one book each to create a massive series (with TWO spin-offs & a collectible card "thing") "Round Robin" style.<br/>The story is good, two kids (Amy and Dan Cahill) find out that they are part of the most influential family in the history of mankind. Then they find out that they are part of the (spoilers!) weakest branch of the family(also known as they "just said no" to "magical" DNA a</span>
  <span id="freeText8168505694540898401" style="display:none">My review is really 4.5 stars for a couple reasons. First, it has a good setup, a bunch of different authors create one book each to create a massive series (with TWO spin-offs &amp; a collectible card "thing") "Round Robin" style.<br />The story is good, two kids (Amy and Dan Cahill) find out that they are part of the most influential family in the history of mankind. Then they find out that they are part of the (spoilers!) weakest branch of the family(also known as they "just said no" to "magical" DNA altering serum of Giddian Cahill that also prevents plague.). But... "Round Robbin" stories can go anywhere, which can lead to great things and HORRIBLE things(but mostly good.) Anddd... so, it's time for some BAD things! Amy and Dan are extremely stupid sometimes. If you are a fan of professor Layton ds games or other logic puzzles, you will practically be shouting "MOBIOS STRIP! MOBIOS STRIP!" or, "it's not a riddle!"<br /><br />Overall this is a good series! BUT don't get addicted to (spoiler) 38 ingredients and recipe because "Cahill's V.S. Vespers" will ruin your respect for this great series.<br /><br />Oh! And look in the inside cover and outside cover for codes! Look hard!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6855922571444102100">Wow, the first ten books in a word? Awesome.<br/><br/>These books kept me sane in midst of exams, projects and heartbreaks.   <span id="freeText6855922571444102100" style="display:none">Wow, the first ten books in a word? Awesome.<br /><br />These books kept me sane in midst of exams, projects and heartbreaks. Take note, this is the review for the whole 10 books, not one by one.<br /><br />If these books sucked, I wouldn't have continued on to the second volume. These ten books are action packed, and funny at times. It even made me cry (at a certain person's death in book 6 and 9.) Dan and Amy are siblings which are competing in a crazy competition against their own kin, and it's do or die. They might be the underdogs- no money, no parents, just each other- but it seems that they have undiscovered tricks up their sleeves. Equipped with nothing but a great Au Pair, Nellie, a cool and spoiled cat, Amy's great researching skills, and Dan's photographic memory, they're ready to take on the world, and their own relatives who can't wait to put a stainless, cold knife to their throats, all because of the powerful secret of The 39 Clues.</span>

<div id="review_453970275" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453970275" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4323315-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491595021p2/4323315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/453970275?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4323315-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4323315-laura?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4323315-laura?shelf=upper-elementary">upper-elementary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer453970275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15344494090027181093">I bought the entire series on eBay. It was popular with many of the quieter students of last year's class so I wanted to see what it was all about.<br/><br/>I am not fond of mysteries but the clues kept me guessing. I was so proud (sad, I know) when I figured out a clue ahead of Dan and Amy. I like that the books taught science, history, and geography to the unwitting readers. I like that the importance of working together was pressed but I'm not sure how I feel about the issue of children working togethe</span>
  <span id="freeText15344494090027181093" style="display:none">I bought the entire series on eBay. It was popular with many of the quieter students of last year's class so I wanted to see what it was all about.<br /><br />I am not fond of mysteries but the clues kept me guessing. I was so proud (sad, I know) when I figured out a clue ahead of Dan and Amy. I like that the books taught science, history, and geography to the unwitting readers. I like that the importance of working together was pressed but I'm not sure how I feel about the issue of children working together in order to defeat their evil parents. I like that people actually got hurt and died; kids need to realize that adventure can be dangerous.<br /><br />I'm going to recommend the series to several of my students. I already have one student who is enthralled by book 1. I'm looking forward to seeing his face when he sees the whole series on my bookshelf.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15344494090027181093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6800852840297596901" style="display:none">Book review Antonella Del Cid, 30 March 2020 <br /> <br />The 39 clues is about a group of friends that enter a contest that they have to find and discover 39 clues. The story does have some twists, in one clue it was about giving someone of the team kicked out and all the other clues were about to stay together and do the tasks together. Who are the characters and what do they represent? Amy is the one that is fun and gives motivation to the group, Dan is shy but he discovers most of the clues because he is really smart and has an open mind, Sydney is the one that does all the dangerous things for the group, and Cahill is the one that takes desitions for the group and tells them where to go and what to do. The most important moments of the book where, when they had to make decisions about what to take and where to go. The book changed me because now I am more creative and think outside the box. I would recommend this book to Zoe Ahunchain because she like intense books. Here is more information and quotes from the book.<br />Quotes: <br /> <br /></span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_11198312'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11198312-the-medusa-plot"><img alt="The Medusa Plot (39 Clues: Cahills vs. Vespers, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1328836311l/11198312._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kVNLvL+lJCPqi1Fdo/i9+10ssqdqOippvTciV+9JNBC6F8h4ZP4a3y9J2TPb3/9Wy0fRolQzeLUYmbSkBvgDbw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('prG+2msfrE5OmBL0fA1/CAym8FyGGT2LtPRdCnV7TQ6N9T0esESSsotampoEKj2lms2TWbgQb1cRWsv5nMp6cQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
